              <span id="reviewTextContainer497192326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15145583158227989122"><b>
  <i>They both knew everything about this moment would change them forever. They both understood there was no<br/>going back.</i>
</b><br/><br/>What an insanely complicated and full-of-twists book. The whole first half of the book was just one mystery after another, and I just wanted to know what Milo's goddamn secrets were! The betrayals, the heartache, the wrong-doings, the love, the happiness and the devastation - well this book just drew me in and spat me right back out.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>"I didn't lie to you. I protected you. Ther</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText15145583158227989122" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>They both knew everything about this moment would change them forever. They both understood there was no<br />going back.</i>
</b><br /><br />What an insanely complicated and full-of-twists book. The whole first half of the book was just one mystery after another, and I just wanted to know what Milo's goddamn secrets were! The betrayals, the heartache, the wrong-doings, the love, the happiness and the devastation - well this book just drew me in and spat me right back out.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"I didn't lie to you. I protected you. There's a difference," Parker said softly, her mouth inches from his.</i>
</b><br /><br />The plot was original, and I definitely loved the unrelenting mystery story that led the way. All the secrets each of the three main characters kept from one another shocked me at every turn, and it left me wanting more.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Every single day for eight years you were the only one I ever wanted to be completely honest with." </i>
</b><br /><br />The heroine was one word.. in a nutshell.. KICKASS. She was just freaking awesome. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I guess that comes with being a CIA agent  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I loved how she didn't take crap from anyone but at the same time showed a bit of vulnerability towards the other characters, Garrett in particular.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Love is a blessing which one can only hope for.</i>
</b><br /><br />Garrett - what character. Selfless, smart, cunning, attractive, loyal, brave - what more could ask for in a leading male. He had me backing him from the very start. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>His brain was at war with his libido, and he wasn't positive which would win or which he wanted to win for that matter.</i>
</b><br /><br />Milo - well he is a complex and effed up character indeed. I will let you read the book to find out just how much for yourself.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>It’s always been you.</i>
</b><br /><br />The love story had bme hooked from the start and I really felt the character's pain when each other's secrets were revealed. Let me tell you know, the wait for the love scene between Garrett and her... was totally worth it. You will not be disappointed. Man that was hot. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Everything I have to give, it’s yours. It’s always been yours.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Recommended for those who like mysteries, betrayals, love stories, love triangles and lots and lots of action. I give it a 4/5!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"If you were mine, I would never be able to walk away from you. If you were mine, I’d wor- ship every inch of your body with my hands, lips, and tongue. If you were mine, I wouldn't be able to stand in the same room as you without running my hands over your skin and tasting your lips. If you were<br />mine..."</i>
</b></span>

<div id="review_439558118" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/439558118" />
    <a title="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5498948-lana-dg-romance"><img alt="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376622739p2/5498948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/439558118?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾" href="/user/show/5498948-lana-dg-romance">Lana ❇✾DG Romance❇✾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17155633-a-beautiful-lie">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=steamy-romance">steamy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=3-stars-or-less-reads">3-stars-or-less-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5498948-lana-dg-romance?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer439558118" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5385214597284151006">Boy oh boy it pains me to do this.<br/><br/>Let me preface this review by saying I love Tara Sivec's writing. Her Chocolate Lovers Series is forever in my favorites shelf. <br/><br/>This is a huge reason why I was so eagerly anticipating the release of this book. I love me some Romantic Suspense...and judging by Ms. Sivec's previous work, I just knew I would love this book.<br/><br/>That's a huge reason, I suppose, of why I'm so disappointed with this book. :(<br/><br/>Let me start off with what I liked:<br/>1.<b> The story itself was great!</b> </span>
  <span id="freeText5385214597284151006" style="display:none">Boy oh boy it pains me to do this.<br /><br />Let me preface this review by saying I love Tara Sivec's writing. Her Chocolate Lovers Series is forever in my favorites shelf. <br /><br />This is a huge reason why I was so eagerly anticipating the release of this book. I love me some Romantic Suspense...and judging by Ms. Sivec's previous work, I just knew I would love this book.<br /><br />That's a huge reason, I suppose, of why I'm so disappointed with this book. :(<br /><br />Let me start off with what I liked:<br />1.<b> The story itself was great!</b> The plot was intense and interesting and the twists kept coming and coming.<br />2. <b> The Characters </b> Garrett, Le Sigh, oh so sexy Garrett. Loved him! and Parker was the ultimate heroine. All the supporting characters were fantastic as well.<br />3. <b> The Romance </b> I loved reading the romance finally develop between Garrett and Parker after so many years of unrequited love. The love scenes?? GOOD GAWD! they.were.HOT!<br /><br />Now what I didn't like:<br /><br />1. <b>The formatting </b> The story flip flopped A LOT, going from past tense, to present tense and back...it made it very hard to keep up with at times due to the formatting of the paragraphs. There was no font change to indicate a change, there was no paragraph indentation or spacing. This became super frustrating for me after a while, since I often would be into the story, and it would switch to 8 years ago, or a few months ago, or a few days or hours ago, without any warning in the writing whatsoever. An italics font would have helped, maybe spacing in the paragraphs between present and past...or I dunno...anything!<br /><br />2. <b> The writing</b> GAH! this was so frustrating for me. I'm not used to this from this author. I loved her previous books, they just flowed for me. The writing was fantastic. It unfolded for the reader almost like a movie. I did not get that with this book. I felt like the author was "telling" me the entire story, as opposed to showing me. At times this frustrated me so much, I just had to put the book down, and it took me longer than usual to finish.<br /><br />3. <b> The transitions </b> ummm..where were they?? There weren't any clear transitions between scenes. Also, the flip flopping between character thoughts; it goes from Parker to Garrett back to Parker to another character like Cole and then back and etc with no clear transition between them. It does this VERY frequently throughout the book. The flow is not smooth and it reads very choppy. I dunno how else to describe it.<br /><br />I feel the problem might have been that Ms. Sivec's previous books (that I've read) were written in first person, and perhaps the transition to 3rd person wasn't as smooth in this novel. Le Sigh.. Either way, it just didn't work for me.<br /><br />There were some editing issues with this book, but for something that cost me $3.99, I really can't complain about it too much. I've seen editing errors be worse in many published books of more well known authors with editors and publishers that cost much more. The editing issue here was mostly lack of spacing between two words like Garrettmoved...and a few other instances.<br /><br />So all in all, it looks as if I'm in the minority once again with my rating of this book among all the great 5 star reviews. <br /><br />To be fair, I'll give it 3 stars, since my issue wasn't with the story but more with the style of writing. <br /><br />I will still read the next book in this series, and keep my fingers crossed that perhaps it will be better. (fingers crossed)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5385214597284151006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_658740236" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/658740236" />
    <a title="Kimberly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21911035-kimberly"><img alt="Kimberly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372968140p2/21911035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/658740236?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kimberly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kimberly" href="/user/show/21911035-kimberly">Kimberly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer658740236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17463967370480007927">Once again I read a book on false claims that it was wonderful! I need to seriously stop reading books based upon their reviews/ratings; this book was HORRIBLE. I think Tara Sivec was in over her head with this one. This book was beyond unbelievable.<br/><br/>I'm not normally into any book that has anything to do with the inner workings of military, CIA, etc., but thought I would give this a go based on it's reviews and book description. Clearly since this isn't a genre/topic I tend to read, I am no exper</span>
  <span id="freeText17463967370480007927" style="display:none">Once again I read a book on false claims that it was wonderful! I need to seriously stop reading books based upon their reviews/ratings; this book was HORRIBLE. I think Tara Sivec was in over her head with this one. This book was beyond unbelievable.<br /><br />I'm not normally into any book that has anything to do with the inner workings of military, CIA, etc., but thought I would give this a go based on it's reviews and book description. Clearly since this isn't a genre/topic I tend to read, I am no expert with anything having to do with CIA, Navy Seals, Black Ops, etc. With that said, upon starting this book, I quickly learned that no extensive knowledge of the topic was necessary to pick up on the unbelievable plot, dialogue, and other various unbelievable happenings of this story.<br /><br />SPOILER ALERT!!!<br /><br />Annabelle meets Milo and Garrett for the first time in a coffee shop her senior year of college, okay- got it. They become close friends, then Annabelle and Milo start dating and eventually become engaged, even though Annabelle really loves Garrett and he her, she pushes those feeling aside because after her mother died, her father fell apart from a broken heart and pushed her away, so she decides she's never going to fully let someone into her heart so she doesn't have to be broken like that. For someone who is supposed to be strong and kick ass, not to mention someone who talks about how all her actions are selfless, this is a very weak and selfish thing to do in my opinion.<br /><br />This is just the tip of the iceberg when it comes to all the things I didn't like about this book. Firstly, I loathed the fact that Garrett called Annabelle - Parker throughout this entire book, while she referred to him rarely by his last name, even though at the beginning of the book the author says they call each other by their last names.<br /><br />I just found the whole "mission" to be very unrealistic. Like I said before, I am no expert, but rarely ever did it seem like these two really had their heads in the game, so to speak. For two people who have as much extensive training as they supposedly had, they sure didn't see that kick ass to me. They were more like children than a Navy SEAL/CIA Black Ops Agent...and on that note, did Annabelle really believe that her friend was killed by the CIA? This is ridiculousness. I realize that Garrett picked up on this quickly, but again, for someone to be so "kick ass" and no even pick up on the this is very unlikely. Her whole photography career was odd too. She became a World renowned photographer in just a few short years after graduating college.<br /><br />Aside from knowing the names of semi-automatic weapons and the fact that she knew she could use her sex appeal to steal another mans weapon, she really didn't seem so kick ass to me.<br /><br />I knew from about the fifth chapter that Milo probably was still alive - it was so typical but written very poorly. The overall flow of the book was terrible too. The flashbacks in the middle of scenes that were already hard to follow anyway, what with the terrible dialogue from the bad guys, and the soft porn from Annabelle and Garrett, it just made it almost impossible to really keep up.<br /><br />So many things, from the way the mission was ran, to the way that Parker and Garrett put the whole mission/fellow agents in jeopardy with their actions, to the God awful dialogue made this book a total dud for me.<br /><br />I honestly didn't even finish this book. After the first half, it just started to drag out. I skimmed through some and just finally skipped to the end after the were both in the basement of the palace at the end. Even when I skipped to the end, I had to skim through that part because it still drug.<br /><br />I really wanted to like this book, really I did. It was just over the top unbelievable and drug out like you wouldn't believe - 1/5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17463967370480007927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/476821479" />
    <a title="Juls" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3381617-juls"><img alt="Juls" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533646876p2/3381617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/476821479?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juls" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juls" href="/user/show/3381617-juls">Juls</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17155633-a-beautiful-lie">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3381617-juls?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3381617-juls?shelf=bad-ass-author">bad-ass-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3381617-juls?shelf=white-book-cover-challenge">white-book-cover-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer476821479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5302735204850317744">You may know Ms Sivec as the author of the Chocolate Lovers Series. I bet you remember how you laughed so hard you pissed a lil in your pants or was unfortunate enough to spray some kind of drink outta your nose. Well put all that aside and prepare yourself. This story takes you on a journey of lies secrets and betrayal your head will spin from all the twists and turns. <br/><br/>Three friends who became family are torn to pieces when they get news of one of their own. <br/>When you think you know the truth ab</span>
  <span id="freeText5302735204850317744" style="display:none">You may know Ms Sivec as the author of the Chocolate Lovers Series. I bet you remember how you laughed so hard you pissed a lil in your pants or was unfortunate enough to spray some kind of drink outta your nose. Well put all that aside and prepare yourself. This story takes you on a journey of lies secrets and betrayal your head will spin from all the twists and turns. <br /><br />Three friends who became family are torn to pieces when they get news of one of their own. <br />When you think you know the truth about Milo you are proven wrong time and time again. When you think you know anything about Parker you really have no idea who or what she is. When you think Garrett should get the girl, you may be right or are you? Can he learn to trust? <br />Friends are hurt and then turn to lovers and when you think you know the truth its only half of what you may think you know. <br /><br />I'm afraid if I gave anymore than I already did in my review I would give away parts and pieces of a story that is just beyond amazing. You really need to read this for yourself to get the full affect. <br /><br />I commend Ms Sivec on a job well done. She wasnt the author of just another funny book but that her talents go far beyond that. She far exceeded my standards with this story. Its definitely a must read! <br /><br />see my review live on Jan 13, 2013 at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.upallnightreviews.blogspot.com">www.upallnightreviews.blogspot.com</a></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('viQNUtVf1W1bGBF8tC1QztglkuIocdtWi5sD1nYi+bZOPqLx62JAr9OP+4BHbWVZ+vTIxDF4gB9fc+lsElsS0Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

I’m sorry it wasn’t me.\n					Lucy\n\nTo get the ending they want, Lucy and Fisher will have to go back to the beginning. When he decides to do something rash and becomes a Navy SEAL, he thinks he\'s finally escaped the rigid structure of the high society life his parents forced down his throat. All he does is trade in one set of rules for another. He follows military protocol to a T, but it still results in the death of an entire team of Navy SEALS and puts his best friends directly in harm\'s way. He’s struggled to stay afloat and not drown in grief, guilt, and booze, but he\'s losing that battle quickly. When his baby sister flees her abusive husband and shows up on his doorstep with his young niece in tow, he has no choice but to clean up his act. He will stop at nothing to protect them and never let them down again, even if it means taking a job that goes against everything he believes in. If protecting a pop star princess who thinks she\'s better than everyone means he can keep a roof over their head, what other choice does he have? \n\nLayla Carlysle has lived a life of luxury. She\'s been a star since the young age of fifteen, and every record she releases shoots straight to the top of the charts. She has people surrounding her every single day telling her how amazing she is, how beautiful she is, and how lucky she is, but she’s never felt more alone in her entire life. She wants nothing more than to break free and do what she really wants to do: write her own music, sing her own songs, and find a way to finally be happy with her life. The only thing standing in her way is her mother, Eve Carlysle. Eve has controlled every single aspect of her daughter’s life and will stop at nothing to achieve fame and fortune, even if that means using her daughter to get there. When an overly-amorous fan’s letters become increasingly more sinister, Brady will have to suck up his opinion of how the other half lives to take the job seriously. The pair will need to learn to trust each other and put aside their differences before the letters become a reality and someone’s life is in jeopardy. \n\nBrady has been to hell and back, and he refuses to let anyone else get close to him again.
